SAMPLE 1
source_split: learn

experiment: 3zSNGrLvJJYZhmW2p
participant: OBSERVER

game_finished: True
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 1.3× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 5.2× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may reward each other.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who rewarded whom.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 3.9× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 1.2× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 1.7× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 11.3× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 8.5× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds, who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.
# GAME STARTS

<ROUND_INFO> Each player starts with 20 coins already in the public fund and chooses how many coins to pull back for private use (equivalently, contribution options are integer from 0 to 20). (multiplier: 8.5×). </ROUND_INFO>

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 3.4× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 4.2× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may reward each other.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who rewarded whom.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 2.8× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 2.0× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 5.9× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 10.0× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 4.9× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may reward each other.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who rewarded whom.

In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 1.8× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 3.7× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 2.2× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 6.2× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 11.5× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 2.6× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 3.7× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including the total number of rounds.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (either 0 or 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 2.9× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including who punished whom, who rewarded whom, and other players' round summaries.

You are observing an online public goods game (PGG) from an omniscient observer's perspective. Each player receives 20 coins per round and chooses how many coins to put into the shared pot (integer from 0 to 20).
In the actual player experience, players do not see others' choices before deciding.
The pot is multiplied by 4.5× and split equally among all active players.
A player's round payoff is: coins kept + equal share of the multiplied pot, adjusted for any punishment or reward outcomes.
After contributions are redistributed, players may punish or reward each other.
At the start of each round, players may optionally send ONE short message to the group.
Observer note: this transcript always includes the full round count, every player's actions, exact punishment/reward source-target identities, and per-player round summaries.
Some of that information was not available to individual players in the live game, including other players' round summaries.
